    <p>\n
    </p>\n
    <h1><a name="name">NAME</a></h1>\n
    <p>BusyBox - The Swiss Army Knife of Embedded Linux</p>\n
    <p>\n
    </p>\n
    <hr>\n
    <h1><a name="syntax">SYNTAX</a></h1>\n
    <pre> BusyBox &lt;function&gt; [arguments...]  # or</pre>\n
    <pre> &lt;function&gt; [arguments...]          # if symlinked</pre>\n
    <p>\n
    </p>\n
    <hr>\n
    <h1><a name="description">DESCRIPTION</a></h1>\n
    <p>BusyBox combines tiny versions of many common UNIX utilities into a single\n
    small executable. It provides minimalist replacements for most of the utilities\n
    you usually find in GNU coreutils, util-linux, etc. The utilities in BusyBox\n
    generally have fewer options than their full-featured GNU cousins; however, the\n
    options that are included provide the expected functionality and behave very\n
    much like their GNU counterparts.</p>\n
    <p>BusyBox has been written with size-optimization and limited resources in mind.\n
    It is also extremely modular so you can easily include or exclude commands (or\n
    features) at compile time. This makes it easy to customize your embedded\n
    systems. To create a working system, just add /dev, /etc, and a Linux kernel.\n
    BusyBox provides a fairly complete POSIX environment for any small or embedded\n
    system.</p>\n
    <p>BusyBox is extremely configurable.  This allows you to include only the\n
    components you need, thereby reducing binary size. Run 'make config' or 'make\n
    menuconfig' to select the functionality that you wish to enable.  Then run\n
    'make' to compile BusyBox using your configuration.</p>\n
    <p>After the compile has finished, you should use 'make install' to install\n
    BusyBox. This will install the 'bin/busybox' binary, in the target directory\n
    specified by CONFIG_PREFIX. CONFIG_PREFIX can be set when configuring BusyBox,\n
    or you can specify an alternative location at install time (i.e., with a\n
    command line like 'make CONFIG_PREFIX=/tmp/foo install'). If you enabled\n
    any applet installation scheme (either as symlinks or hardlinks), these will\n
    also be installed in the location pointed to by CONFIG_PREFIX.</p>\n
    <p>\n
    </p>\n
    <hr>\n
    <h1><a name="usage">USAGE</a></h1>\n
    <p>BusyBox is a multi-call binary.  A multi-call binary is an executable program\n
    that performs the same job as more than one utility program.  That means there\n
    is just a single BusyBox binary, but that single binary acts like a large\n
    number of utilities.  This allows BusyBox to be smaller since all the built-in\n
    utility programs (we call them applets) can share code for many common operations.</p>\n
    <p>You can also invoke BusyBox by issuing a command as an argument on the\n
    command line.  For example, entering</p>\n
    <pre>        /bin/busybox ls</pre>\n
    <p>will also cause BusyBox to behave as 'ls'.</p>\n
    <p>Of course, adding '/bin/busybox' into every command would be painful.  So most\n
    people will invoke BusyBox using links to the BusyBox binary.</p>\n
    <p>For example, entering</p>\n
    <pre>        ln -s /bin/busybox ls\n
            ./ls</pre>\n
    <p>will cause BusyBox to behave as 'ls' (if the 'ls' command has been compiled\n
    into BusyBox).  Generally speaking, you should never need to make all these\n
    links yourself, as the BusyBox build system will do this for you when you run\n
    the 'make install' command.</p>\n
    <p>If you invoke BusyBox with no arguments, it will provide you with a list of the\n
    applets that have been compiled into your BusyBox binary.</p>\n
    <p>\n
    </p>\n
    <hr>\n
    <h1><a name="common_options">COMMON OPTIONS</a></h1>\n
    <p>Most BusyBox commands support the <strong>--help</strong> argument to provide a terse runtime\n
    description of their behavior.  If the CONFIG_FEATURE_VERBOSE_USAGE option has\n
    been enabled, more detailed usage information will also be available.</p>\n
    <p>\n
    </p>\n
    <hr>\n

            usleep, uudecode, uuencode, vconfig, vi, vlock, watch, watchdog, \n
            wc, wget, which, who, whoami, xargs, yes, zcat, zcip</pre>\n
    <p>\n
    </p>\n
    <hr>\n
    <h1><a name="command_descriptions">COMMAND DESCRIPTIONS</a></h1>\n
    <dl>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_addgroup"><strong>addgroup  </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    addgroup   [<strong>-g</strong> GID] [user_name] group_name\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Add a group to the system or add an user to a group</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -g GID  Group id</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_adduser"><strong>adduser   </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    adduser    [OPTIONS] user_name\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Add a user to the system</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -h DIR          Home directory\n
            -g GECOS        GECOS field\n
            -s SHELL        Login shell\n
            -G GROUP        Add user to existing group\n
            -S              Create a system user (ignored)\n
            -D              Do not assign a password\n
            -H              Do not create home directory</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_adjtimex"><strong>adjtimex  </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    adjtimex   [<strong>-q</strong>] [<strong>-o</strong> offset] [<strong>-f</strong> frequency] [<strong>-p</strong> timeconstant] [<strong>-t</strong> tick]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Read and optionally set system timebase parameters.\n
    See adjtimex(2).</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -q              Quiet\n
            -o offset       Time offset, microseconds\n
            -f frequency    Frequency adjust, integer kernel units (65536 is 1ppm)\n
                            (positive values make clock run faster)\n
            -t tick         Microseconds per tick, usually 10000\n
            -p timeconstant</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_ar"><strong>ar        </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    ar         [<strong>-o</strong>] [<strong>-v</strong>] [<strong>-p</strong>] [<strong>-t</strong>] [<strong>-x</strong>] ARCHIVE FILES\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Extract or list FILES from an ar archive</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -o      Preserve original dates\n
            -p      Extract to stdout\n
            -t      List\n
            -x      Extract\n
            -v      Verbose</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_arp"><strong>arp       </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"><tbody><tr><td>arp        \n
    </td></tr><tr><td>[<strong>-vn</strong>]</td><td>[<strong>-H</strong> type] [<strong>-i</strong> if] <strong>-a</strong> [hostname]\n
    </td></tr><tr><td>[<strong>-v</strong>]</td><td>  [<strong>-i</strong> if] <strong>-d</strong> hostname [pub]\n
    </td></tr><tr><td>[<strong>-v</strong>]</td><td>[<strong>-H</strong> type] [<strong>-i</strong> if] <strong>-s</strong> hostname hw_addr [temp]\n
    </td></tr><tr><td>[<strong>-v</strong>]</td><td>[<strong>-H</strong> type] [<strong>-i</strong> if] <strong>-s</strong> hostname hw_addr [netmask nm] pub\n
    </td></tr><tr><td>[<strong>-v</strong>]</td><td>[<strong>-H</strong> type] [<strong>-i</strong> if] <strong>-Ds</strong> hostname ifa [netmask nm] pub</td></tr></tbody></table>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Manipulate the system ARP cache</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -a              Display (all) hosts\n
            -s              Set a new ARP entry\n
            -d              Delete a specified entry\n
            -v              Verbose\n
            -n              Don't resolve names\n
            -i if           Network interface (e.g. eth0)\n
            -D              Read &lt;hwaddr&gt; from given device\n
            -A, -p          Protocol family\n
            -H hwtype       Hardware address type</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_arping"><strong>arping    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    arping     [<strong>-fqbDUA</strong>] [<strong>-c</strong> count] [<strong>-w</strong> timeout] [<strong>-i</strong> device] [<strong>-s</strong> sender] target\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Ping hosts by ARP requests/replies</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -f              Quit on first ARP reply\n
            -q              Quiet\n
            -b              Keep broadcasting, don't go unicast\n
            -D              Duplicated address detection mode\n
            -U              Unsolicited ARP mode, update your neighbours\n
            -A              ARP answer mode, update your neighbours\n
            -c count        Stop after sending count ARP request packets\n
            -w timeout      Time to wait for ARP reply, in seconds\n
            -I device       Outgoing interface name, default is eth0\n
            -s sender       Set specific sender IP address\n
            target          Target IP address of ARP request</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_ash"><strong>ash       </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    ash        [FILE]...\n
    or: ash <strong>-c</strong> command [args]...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>The ash shell (command interpreter)</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_awk"><strong>awk       </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    awk        [OPTION]... [program-text] [FILE ...]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -v var=val      Set variable\n
            -F sep          Use sep as field separator\n
            -f filename     Read program from file</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_basename"><strong>basename  </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    basename   FILE [SUFFIX]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Strip directory path and suffixes from FILE.\n
    If specified, also remove any trailing SUFFIX.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ basename /usr/local/bin/foo\n
            foo\n
            $ basename /usr/local/bin/\n
            bin\n
            $ basename /foo/bar.txt .txt\n
            bar</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_bbconfig"><strong>bbconfig  </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    bbconfig\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Print the config file which built busybox</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n

    or: bbsh <strong>-c</strong> command [args]...\n

    bunzip2    [OPTION]... [FILE]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Uncompress FILE (or standard input if FILE is '-' or omitted)</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n

            -f      Force</pre>\n
    </dd>\n

    <dt><strong><a name="item_cal"><strong>cal       </strong></a></strong><br>\n

    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Display a calendar</p>\n

    </dd>\n

    <pre>        -j      Use julian dates\n
            -y      Display the entire year</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_cat"><strong>cat       </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    cat        [<strong>-u</strong>] [FILE]...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Concatenate <code>FILE(s)</code> and print them to stdout</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -u      Use unbuffered i/o (ignored)</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ cat /proc/uptime\n
            110716.72 17.67</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_catv"><strong>catv      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    catv       [<strong>-etv</strong>] [FILE]...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Display nonprinting characters as ^x or M-x</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -e      End each line with $\n
            -t      Show tabs as ^I\n
            -v      Don't use ^x or M-x escapes</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_chattr"><strong>chattr    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    chattr     [<strong>-R</strong>] [-+=AacDdijsStTu] [<strong>-v</strong> version] files...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Change file attributes on an ext2 fs</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Modifiers:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -       Remove attributes\n
            +       Add attributes\n
            =       Set attributes\n
    Attributes:</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        A       Don't track atime\n
            a       Append mode only\n
            c       Enable compress\n
            D       Write dir contents synchronously\n
            d       Do not backup with dump\n
            i       Cannot be modified (immutable)\n
            j       Write all data to journal first\n
            s       Zero disk storage when deleted\n
            S       Write file contents synchronously\n
            t       Disable tail-merging of partial blocks with other files\n
            u       Allow file to be undeleted\n
    Options:</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -R      Recursively list subdirectories\n
            -v      Set the file's version/generation number</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_chcon"><strong>chcon     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"><tbody><tr><td>chcon      [OPTIONS] CONTEXT FILE...\n
    </td></tr><tr><td></td><td>chcon [OPTIONS] [<strong>-u</strong> USER] [<strong>-r</strong> ROLE] [<strong>-l</strong> RANGE] [<strong>-t</strong> TYPE] FILE...\n
    </td></tr><tr><td></td><td>chcon [OPTIONS] -<strong>-reference</strong>=RFILE FILE...</td></tr></tbody></table>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Change the security context of each FILE to CONTEXT</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -v, --verbose           Verbose\n
            -c, --changes           Report changes made\n
            -h, --no-dereference    Affect symlinks instead of their targets\n
            -f, --silent, --quiet   Suppress most error messages\n
            --reference=RFILE       Use RFILE's group instead of using a CONTEXT value\n
            -u, --user=USER         Set user USER in the target security context\n
            -r, --role=ROLE         Set role ROLE in the target security context\n
            -t, --type=TYPE         Set type TYPE in the target security context\n
            -l, --range=RANGE       Set range RANGE in the target security context\n
            -R, --recursive         Recurse subdirectories</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_chgrp"><strong>chgrp     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    chgrp      [<strong>-RhLHPcvf</strong>]... GROUP FILE...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Change the group membership of each FILE to GROUP</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -R      Recurse directories\n
            -h      Affect symlinks instead of symlink targets\n
            -L      Traverse all symlinks to directories\n
            -H      Traverse symlinks on command line only\n
            -P      Do not traverse symlinks (default)\n
            -c      List changed files\n
            -v      Verbose\n
            -f      Hide errors</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ ls -l /tmp/foo\n
            -r--r--r--    1 andersen andersen        0 Apr 12 18:25 /tmp/foo\n
            $ chgrp root /tmp/foo\n
            $ ls -l /tmp/foo\n
            -r--r--r--    1 andersen root            0 Apr 12 18:25 /tmp/foo</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_chmod"><strong>chmod     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    chmod      [<strong>-Rcvf</strong>] MODE[,MODE]... FILE...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Each MODE is one or more of the letters ugoa, one of the\n
    symbols +-= and one or more of the letters rwxst</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -R      Recurse directories\n
            -c      List changed files\n
            -v      List all files\n
            -f      Hide errors</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ ls -l /tmp/foo\n
            -rw-rw-r--    1 root     root            0 Apr 12 18:25 /tmp/foo\n
            $ chmod u+x /tmp/foo\n
            $ ls -l /tmp/foo\n
            -rwxrw-r--    1 root     root            0 Apr 12 18:25 /tmp/foo*\n
            $ chmod 444 /tmp/foo\n
            $ ls -l /tmp/foo\n
            -r--r--r--    1 root     root            0 Apr 12 18:25 /tmp/foo</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_chown"><strong>chown     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    chown      [<strong>-RhLHPcvf</strong>]... OWNER[&lt;.|:&gt;[GROUP]] FILE...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Change the owner and/or group of each FILE to OWNER and/or GROUP</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -R      Recurse directories\n
            -h      Affect symlinks instead of symlink targets\n
            -L      Traverse all symlinks to directories\n
            -H      Traverse symlinks on command line only\n
            -P      Do not traverse symlinks (default)\n
            -c      List changed files\n
            -v      List all files\n
            -f      Hide errors</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ ls -l /tmp/foo\n
            -r--r--r--    1 andersen andersen        0 Apr 12 18:25 /tmp/foo\n
            $ chown root /tmp/foo\n
            $ ls -l /tmp/foo\n
            -r--r--r--    1 root     andersen        0 Apr 12 18:25 /tmp/foo\n
            $ chown root.root /tmp/foo\n
            ls -l /tmp/foo\n
            -r--r--r--    1 root     root            0 Apr 12 18:25 /tmp/foo</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_chpasswd"><strong>chpasswd  </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    chpasswd   [-<strong>-md5</strong>|-<strong>-encrypt</strong>]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Read user:password information from stdin\n
    and update /etc/passwd accordingly.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -e, --encrypt   Supplied passwords are in encrypted form\n
            -m, --md5       Use MD5 encryption instead of DES</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_chpst"><strong>chpst     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    chpst      [<strong>-vP012</strong>] [<strong>-u</strong> user[:group]] [<strong>-U</strong> user[:group]] [<strong>-e</strong> dir] [-/ dir] [<strong>-n</strong> nice] [<strong>-m</strong> bytes] [<strong>-d</strong> bytes] [<strong>-o</s
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Change the process state and run specified program</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -u user[:grp]   Set uid and gid\n
            -U user[:grp]   Set environment variables UID and GID\n
            -e dir          Set environment variables as specified by files\n
                            in the directory: file=1st_line_of_file\n
            -/ dir          Chroot to dir\n
            -n inc          Add inc to nice value\n
            -m bytes        Limit data segment, stack segment, locked physical pages,\n
                            and total of all segment per process to bytes bytes each\n
            -d bytes        Limit data segment\n
            -o n            Limit the number of open file descriptors per process to n\n
            -p n            Limit number of processes per uid to n\n
            -f bytes        Limit output file size to bytes bytes\n
            -c bytes        Limit core file size to bytes bytes\n
            -v              Verbose\n
            -P              Run prog in a new process group\n
            -0              Close standard input\n
            -1              Close standard output\n
            -2              Close standard error</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_chroot"><strong>chroot    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    chroot     NEWROOT [COMMAND...]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Run COMMAND with root directory set to NEWROOT</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ ls -l /bin/ls\n
            lrwxrwxrwx    1 root     root          12 Apr 13 00:46 /bin/ls -&gt; /BusyBox\n
            # mount /dev/hdc1 /mnt -t minix\n
            # chroot /mnt\n
            # ls -l /bin/ls\n
            -rwxr-xr-x    1 root     root        40816 Feb  5 07:45 /bin/ls*</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_chrt"><strong>chrt      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    chrt       [OPTION]... [prio] [pid | command [arg]...]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>manipulate real-time attributes of a process</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -p      operate on pid\n
            -r      set scheduling policy to SCHED_RR\n
            -f      set scheduling policy to SCHED_FIFO\n
            -o      set scheduling policy to SCHED_OTHER\n
            -m      show min and max priorities</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ chrt -r 4 sleep 900; x=$!\n
            $ chrt -f -p 3 $x\n
            You need CAP_SYS_NICE privileges to set scheduling attributes of a process</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_chvt"><strong>chvt      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    chvt       N\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Change the foreground virtual terminal to /dev/ttyN</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_cksum"><strong>cksum     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    cksum      FILES...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Calculate the CRC32 checksums of FILES</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_clear"><strong>clear     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    clear\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Clear screen</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_cmp"><strong>cmp       </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    cmp        [<strong>-l</strong>] [<strong>-s</strong>] FILE1 [FILE2 [SKIP1 [SKIP2]]]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Compares FILE1 vs stdin if FILE2 is not specified</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -l      Write the byte numbers (decimal) and values (octal)\n
                    for all differing bytes\n
            -s      Quiet</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_comm"><strong>comm      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    comm       [<strong>-123</strong>] FILE1 FILE2\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Compare FILE1 to FILE2, or to stdin if - is specified</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -1      Suppress lines unique to FILE1\n
            -2      Suppress lines unique to FILE2\n
            -3      Suppress lines common to both files</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_cp"><strong>cp        </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    cp         [OPTION]... SOURCE DEST\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Copy SOURCE to DEST, or multiple <code>SOURCE(s)</code> to DIRECTORY</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -a      Same as -dpR\n
            -c      Preserves security context\n
            -d,-P   Preserve links\n
            -H,-L   Dereference all symlinks (default)\n
            -p      Preserve file attributes if possible\n
            -f      Force overwrite\n
            -i      Prompt before overwrite\n
            -R,-r   Recurse directories\n
            -l,-s   Create (sym)links</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_cpio"><strong>cpio      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    cpio       -[dimtuv][F cpiofile]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Extract or list files from a cpio archive\n
    Main operation mode:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        d       Make leading directories\n
            i       Extract\n
            m       Preserve mtime\n
            t       List\n
            v       Verbose\n
            u       Unconditional overwrite\n
            F       Input from file</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_crond"><strong>crond     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n

    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -d [#] -l [#] -S -L logfile -f -b -c dir\n
            -d num  Debug level\n
            -l num  Log level (8 - default)\n
            -S      Log to syslogd (default)\n
            -L file Log to file\n
            -f      Run in foreground\n
            -b      Run in background (default)\n
            -c dir  Working dir</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_crontab"><strong>crontab   </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    crontab    [<strong>-c</strong> dir] {file|-}|[<strong>-u</strong>|<strong>-l</strong>|<strong>-e</strong>|<strong>-d</strong> user]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        file [opts]     Replace crontab from file\n
            - [opts]        Replace crontab from stdin\n
            -u user         User\n
            -l [user]       List crontab for user\n
            -e [user]       Edit crontab for user\n
            -d [user]       Delete crontab for user\n
            -c dir          Crontab directory</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_cryptpw"><strong>cryptpw   </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    cryptpw    [<strong>-a</strong> des|md5] [string]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Outputs crypted string.\n
    If string isn't supplied on cmdline, reads it from stdin.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -a      Algorithm to use (default: md5)</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_cut"><strong>cut       </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    cut        [OPTION]... [FILE]...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Print selected fields from each input FILE to standard output</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -b LIST Output only bytes from LIST\n
            -c LIST Output only characters from LIST\n
            -d CHAR Use CHAR instead of tab as the field delimiter\n
            -s      Output only the lines containing delimiter\n
            -f N    Print only these fields\n
            -n      Ignored</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ echo "Hello world" | cut -f 1 -d ' '\n
            Hello\n
            $ echo "Hello world" | cut -f 2 -d ' '\n
            world</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_date"><strong>date      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    date       [OPTION]... [MMDDhhmm[[CC]YY][.ss]] [+FORMAT]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Display current time in the given FORMAT, or set system date</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -R              Outputs RFC-822 compliant date string\n
            -d STRING       Displays time described by STRING, not 'now'\n
            -I[TIMESPEC]    Outputs an ISO-8601 compliant date/time string\n
                            TIMESPEC='date' (or missing) for date only,\n
                            'hours', 'minutes', or 'seconds' for date and\n
                            time to the indicated precision\n
            -D hint         Use 'hint' as date format, via strptime()\n
            -s STRING       Sets time described by STRING\n
            -r FILE         Displays the last modification time of FILE\n
            -u              Prints or sets Coordinated Universal Time</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ date\n
            Wed Apr 12 18:52:41 MDT 2000</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_dc"><strong>dc        </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    dc         expression ...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>This is a Tiny RPN calculator that understands the\n
    following operations: +, add, -, sub, *, mul, /, div, %, mod, **, exp, and, or, not, eor.\n
    For example: 'dc 2 2 add' -&gt; 4, and 'dc 8 8 \* 2 2 + /' -&gt; 16.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:\n
    p - Prints the value on the top of the stack, without altering the stack\n
    f - Prints the entire contents of the stack without altering anything\n
    o - Pops the value off the top of the stack and uses it to set the output radix</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>    Only 10 and 16 are supported</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ dc 2 2 + p\n
            4\n
            $ dc 8 8 \* 2 2 + / p\n
            16\n
            $ dc 0 1 and p\n
            0\n
            $ dc 0 1 or p\n
            1\n
            $ echo 72 9 div 8 mul p | dc\n
            64</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_dd"><strong>dd        </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"><tbody><tr><td>dd         [if=FILE] [of=FILE] [ibs=N] [obs=N] [bs=N] [count=N] [skip=N]\n
    </td></tr><tr><td></td><td>[seek=N] [conv=notrunc|noerror|sync]</td></tr></tbody></table>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Copy a file with converting and formatting</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        if=FILE         Read from FILE instead of stdin\n
            of=FILE         Write to FILE instead of stdout\n
            bs=N            Read and write N bytes at a time\n
            ibs=N           Read N bytes at a time\n
            obs=N           Write N bytes at a time\n
            count=N         Copy only N input blocks\n
            skip=N          Skip N input blocks\n
            seek=N          Skip N output blocks\n
            conv=notrunc    Don't truncate output file\n
            conv=noerror    Continue after read errors\n
            conv=sync       Pad blocks with zeros</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Numbers may be suffixed by c (x1), w (x2), b (x512), kD (x1000), k (x1024),\n
    MD (x1000000), M (x1048576), GD (x1000000000) or G (x1073741824)</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ dd if=/dev/zero of=/dev/ram1 bs=1M count=4\n
            4+0 records in\n
            4+0 records out</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n

    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    diff       [<strong>-abdiNqrTstw</strong>] [<strong>-L</strong> LABEL] [<strong>-S</strong> FILE] [<strong>-U</strong> LINES] FILE1 FILE2\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Compare files line by line and output the differences between them.\n
    This diff implementation only supports unified diffs.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -a      Treat all files as text\n
            -b      Ignore changes in the amount of whitespace\n
            -d      Try hard to find a smaller set of changes\n
            -i      Ignore case differences\n
            -L      Use LABEL instead of the filename in the unified header\n
            -N      Treat absent files as empty\n
            -q      Output only whether files differ\n
            -r      Recursively compare subdirectories\n
            -S      Start with FILE when comparing directories\n
            -T      Make tabs line up by prefixing a tab when necessary\n
            -s      Report when two files are the same\n
            -t      Expand tabs to spaces in output\n
            -U      Output LINES lines of context\n
            -w      Ignore all whitespace</pre>\n
    </dd>\n

    <dt><strong><a name="item_du"><strong>du        </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    du         [<strong>-aHLdclsxhmk</strong>] [FILE]...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Summarize disk space used for each FILE and/or directory.\n
    Disk space is printed in units of 1024 bytes.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -a      Show sizes of files in addition to directories\n
            -H      Follow symlinks that are FILE command line args\n
            -L      Follow all symlinks encountered\n
            -d N    Limit output to directories (and files with -a) of depth &lt; N\n
            -c      Output a grand total\n
            -l      Count sizes many times if hard linked\n
            -s      Display only a total for each argument\n
            -x      Skip directories on different filesystems\n
            -h      Print sizes in human readable format (e.g., 1K 243M 2G )\n
            -m      Print sizes in megabytes\n
            -k      Print sizes in kilobytes(default)</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ du\n
            16      ./CVS\n
            12      ./kernel-patches/CVS\n
            80      ./kernel-patches\n
            12      ./tests/CVS\n
            36      ./tests\n
            12      ./scripts/CVS\n
            16      ./scripts\n
            12      ./docs/CVS\n
            104     ./docs\n
            2417    .</pre>\n
    </dd>\n

    <dt><strong><a name="item_ether_wake"><strong>ether_wake</strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    ether_wake [<strong>-b</strong>] [<strong>-i</strong> iface] [<strong>-p</strong> aa:bb:cc:dd[:ee:ff]] MAC\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Send a magic packet to wake up sleeping machines.\n
    MAC must be a station address (00:11:22:33:44:55) or\n
    a hostname with a known 'ethers' entry.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -b              Send wake-up packet to the broadcast address\n
            -i iface        Use interface ifname instead of the default "eth0"\n
            -p pass         Append the four or six byte password PW to the packet</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_expand"><strong>expand    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    expand     [<strong>-i</strong>] [<strong>-t</strong> NUM] [FILE|-]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Convert tabs to spaces, writing to standard output.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -i,--initial    Do not convert tabs after non blanks\n
            -t,--tabs=N     Tabstops every N chars</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_expr"><strong>expr      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    expr       EXPRESSION\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Print the value of EXPRESSION to standard output.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>EXPRESSION may be:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        ARG1 |  ARG2    ARG1 if it is neither null nor 0, otherwise ARG2\n
            ARG1 &amp;  ARG2    ARG1 if neither argument is null or 0, otherwise 0\n
            ARG1 &lt;  ARG2    ARG1 is less than ARG2\n
            ARG1 &lt;= ARG2    ARG1 is less than or equal to ARG2\n
            ARG1 =  ARG2    ARG1 is equal to ARG2\n
            ARG1 != ARG2    ARG1 is unequal to ARG2\n
            ARG1 &gt;= ARG2    ARG1 is greater than or equal to ARG2\n
            ARG1 &gt;  ARG2    ARG1 is greater than ARG2\n
            ARG1 +  ARG2    Sum of ARG1 and ARG2\n
            ARG1 -  ARG2    Difference of ARG1 and ARG2\n
            ARG1 *  ARG2    Product of ARG1 and ARG2\n
            ARG1 /  ARG2    Quotient of ARG1 divided by ARG2\n
            ARG1 %  ARG2    Remainder of ARG1 divided by ARG2\n
            STRING : REGEXP         Anchored pattern match of REGEXP in STRING\n
            match STRING REGEXP     Same as STRING : REGEXP\n
            substr STRING POS LENGTH Substring of STRING, POS counted from 1\n
            index STRING CHARS      Index in STRING where any CHARS is found, or 0\n
            length STRING           Length of STRING\n
            quote TOKEN             Interpret TOKEN as a string, even if\n
                                    it is a keyword like 'match' or an\n
                                    operator like '/'\n
            (EXPRESSION)            Value of EXPRESSION</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Beware that many operators need to be escaped or quoted for shells.\n
    Comparisons are arithmetic if both ARGs are numbers, else\n
    lexicographical. Pattern matches return the string matched between\n
    \( and \) or null; if \( and \) are not used, they return the number\n
    of characters matched or 0.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_fakeidentd"><strong>fakeidentd</strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    fakeidentd [<strong>-fiw</strong>] [<strong>-b</strong> ADDR] [STRING]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Provide fake ident (auth) service</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -f      Run in foreground\n
            -i      Inetd mode\n
            -w      Inetd 'wait' mode\n
            -b ADDR Bind to specified address\n
            STRING  Ident answer string (default is 'nobody')</pre>\n
    </dd>\n

    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    fdisk      [<strong>-luv</strong>] [<strong>-C</strong> CYLINDERS] [<strong>-H</strong> HEADS] [<strong>-S</strong> SECTORS] [<strong>-b</strong> SSZ] DISK\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n

    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -l              List partition table(s)\n
            -u              Give Start and End in sector (instead of cylinder) units\n
            -s PARTITION    Give partition size(s) in blocks\n
            -b 2048         (for certain MO disks) use 2048-byte sectors\n
            -C CYLINDERS    Set the number of cylinders\n
            -H HEADS        Set the number of heads\n
            -S SECTORS      Set the number of sectors\n
            -v              Give fdisk version</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_find"><strong>find      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    find       [PATH...] [EXPRESSION]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Search for files in a directory hierarchy. The default PATH is\n
    the current directory, default EXPRESSION is '<strong>-print</strong>'</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>EXPRESSION may consist of:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -follow         Dereference symlinks\n
            -xdev           Don't descend directories on other filesystems\n
            -maxdepth N     Descend at most N levels. -maxdepth 0 applies\n
                            tests/actions to command line arguments only\n
            -name PATTERN   File name (w/o directory name) matches PATTERN\n
            -path PATTERN   Path matches PATTERN\n
            -regex PATTERN  Path matches regex PATTERN\n
            -type X         File type is X (X is one of: f,d,l,b,c,...)\n
            -perm NNN       Permissions match any of (+NNN), all of (-NNN),\n
                            or exactly (NNN)\n
            -mtime DAYS     Modified time is greater than (+N), less than (-N),\n
                            or exactly (N) days\n
            -mmin MINS      Modified time is greater than (+N), less than (-N),\n
                            or exactly (N) minutes\n
            -newer FILE     Modified time is more recent than FILE's\n
            -inum N         File has inode number N\n
            -user NAME      File is owned by user NAME (numeric user ID allowed)\n
            -group NAME     File belongs to group NAME (numeric group ID allowed)\n
            -depth          Process directory name after traversing it\n
            -size N[bck]    File size is N (c:bytes,k:kbytes,b:512 bytes(def.)).\n
                            +/-N: file size is bigger/smaller than N\n
            -print          Print (default and assumed)\n
            -print0         Delimit output with null characters rather than\n
                            newlines        USE_FEATURE_FIND_CONTEXT ( \n
            -context        File has specified security context")    \n
            -exec CMD ARG ; Execute CMD with all instances of {} replaced by the\n
                            matching files\n
            -prune          Stop traversing current subtree\n
            -delete         Delete files, turns on -depth option\n
            (EXPR)          Group an expression</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ find / -name passwd\n
            /etc/passwd</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_fold"><strong>fold      </strong></a></strong><br>\n

    <dt><strong><a name="item_getenforce"><strong>getenforce</strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n

    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_getopt"><strong>getopt    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    getopt     [OPTIONS]...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Parse command options</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -a, --alternative               Allow long options starting with single -\n
            -l, --longoptions=longopts      Long options to be recognized\n
            -n, --name=progname             The name under which errors are reported\n
            -o, --options=optstring         Short options to be recognized\n
            -q, --quiet                     Disable error reporting by getopt(3)\n
            -Q, --quiet-output              No normal output\n
            -s, --shell=shell               Set shell quoting conventions\n
            -T, --test                      Test for getopt(1) version\n
            -u, --unquoted                  Do not quote the output</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ cat getopt.test\n
            #!/bin/sh\n
            GETOPT=`getopt -o ab:c:: --long a-long,b-long:,c-long:: \\n
                   -n 'example.busybox' -- "$@"`\n
            if [ $? != 0 ]; then  exit 1; fi\n
            eval set -- "$GETOPT"\n
            while true; do\n
             case $1 in\n
               -a|--a-long) echo "Option a"; shift;;\n
               -b|--b-long) echo "Option b, argument '$2'"; shift 2;;\n
               -c|--c-long)\n
                 case "$2" in\n
                   "") echo "Option c, no argument"; shift 2;;\n
                   *)  echo "Option c, argument '$2'"; shift 2;;\n
                 esac;;\n
               --) shift; break;;\n
               *) echo "Internal error!"; exit 1;;\n
             esac\n
            done</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_getsebool"><strong>getsebool </strong></a></strong><br>\n

    <dt><strong><a name="item_getty"><strong>getty     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    getty      [OPTIONS]... baud_rate,... line [termtype]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Open a tty, prompt for a login name, then invoke /bin/login</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -h              Enable hardware (RTS/CTS) flow control\n
            -i              Do not display /etc/issue before running login\n
            -L              Local line, so do not do carrier detect\n
            -m              Get baud rate from modem's CONNECT status message\n
            -w              Wait for a CR or LF before sending /etc/issue\n
            -n              Do not prompt the user for a login name\n
            -f issue_file   Display issue_file instead of /etc/issue\n
            -l login_app    Invoke login_app instead of /bin/login\n
            -t timeout      Terminate after timeout if no username is read\n
            -I initstring   Sets the init string to send before anything else\n
            -H login_host   Log login_host into the utmp file as the hostname</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_grep"><strong>grep      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    grep       [<strong>-HhrilLnqvsoweFEABC</strong>] PATTERN [FILEs...]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Search for PATTERN in each FILE or standard input</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -H      Prefix output lines with filename where match was found\n
            -h      Suppress the prefixing filename on output\n
            -r      Recurse subdirectories\n
            -i      Ignore case distinctions\n
            -l      List names of files that match\n
            -L      List names of files that do not match\n
            -n      Print line number with output lines\n
            -q      Quiet. Returns 0 if PATTERN was found, 1 otherwise\n
            -v      Select non-matching lines\n
            -s      Suppress file open/read error messages\n
            -c      Only print count of matching lines\n
            -o      Show only the part of a line that matches PATTERN\n
            -m MAX  Match up to MAX times per file\n
            -w      Match whole words only\n
            -F      PATTERN is a set of newline-separated strings\n
            -E      PATTERN is an extended regular expression\n
            -e PTRN Pattern to match\n
            -f FILE Read pattern from file\n
            -A      Print NUM lines of trailing context\n
            -B      Print NUM lines of leading context\n
            -C      Print NUM lines of output context</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ grep root /etc/passwd\n
            root:x:0:0:root:/root:/bin/bash\n
            $ grep ^[rR]oo. /etc/passwd\n
            root:x:0:0:root:/root:/bin/bash</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_gunzip"><strong>gunzip    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    gunzip     [OPTION]... FILE\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Uncompress FILE (or standard input if FILE is '-')</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -c      Write output to standard output\n
            -f      Force read when source is a terminal\n
            -t      Test compressed file integrity</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ ls -la /tmp/BusyBox*\n
            -rw-rw-r--    1 andersen andersen   557009 Apr 11 10:55 /tmp/BusyBox-0.43.tar.gz\n
            $ gunzip /tmp/BusyBox-0.43.tar.gz\n
            $ ls -la /tmp/BusyBox*\n
            -rw-rw-r--    1 andersen andersen  1761280 Apr 14 17:47 /tmp/BusyBox-0.43.tar</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_gzip"><strong>gzip      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    gzip       [OPTION]... [FILE]...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Compress <code>FILE(s)</code> with maximum compression.\n
    When FILE is '-' or unspecified, reads standard input. Implies <strong>-c</strong>.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -c      Write output to standard output instead of FILE.gz\n
            -d      Decompress\n
            -f      Force write when destination is a terminal</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ ls -la /tmp/busybox*\n
            -rw-rw-r--    1 andersen andersen  1761280 Apr 14 17:47 /tmp/busybox.tar\n
            $ gzip /tmp/busybox.tar\n
            $ ls -la /tmp/busybox*\n
            -rw-rw-r--    1 andersen andersen   554058 Apr 14 17:49 /tmp/busybox.tar.gz</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_halt"><strong>halt      </strong></a></strong><br>\n

    </dd>\n

            -n      No call to sync()\n

    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_hdparm"><strong>hdparm    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    hdparm     [options] [device] ..\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>         If no device name is specified try to read from stdin.</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -a      Get/set fs readahead\n
            -A      Set drive read-lookahead flag (0/1)\n
            -b      Get/set bus state (0 == off, 1 == on, 2 == tristate)\n
            -B      Set Advanced Power Management setting (1-255)\n
            -c      Get/set IDE 32-bit IO setting\n
            -C      Check IDE power mode status\n
            -d      Get/set using_dma flag\n
            -D      Enable/disable drive defect-mgmt\n
            -f      Flush buffer cache for device on exit\n
            -g      Display drive geometry\n
            -h      Display terse usage information\n
            -i      Display drive identification\n
            -I      Detailed/current information directly from drive\n
            -k      Get/set keep_settings_over_reset flag (0/1)\n
            -K      Set drive keep_features_over_reset flag (0/1)\n
            -L      Set drive doorlock (0/1) (removable harddisks only)\n
            -m      Get/set multiple sector count\n
            -n      Get/set ignore-write-errors flag (0/1)\n
            -p      Set PIO mode on IDE interface chipset (0,1,2,3,4,...)\n
            -P      Set drive prefetch count\n
            -q      Change next setting quietly\n
            -Q      Get/set DMA tagged-queuing depth (if supported)\n
            -r      Get/set readonly flag (DANGEROUS to set)\n
            -R      Register an IDE interface (DANGEROUS)\n
            -S      Set standby (spindown) timeout\n
            -t      Perform device read timings\n
            -T      Perform cache read timings\n
            -u      Get/set unmaskirq flag (0/1)\n
            -U      Un-register an IDE interface (DANGEROUS)\n
            -v      Defaults; same as -mcudkrag for IDE drives\n
            -V      Display program version and exit immediately\n
            -w      Perform device reset (DANGEROUS)\n
            -W      Set drive write-caching flag (0/1) (DANGEROUS)\n
            -x      Tristate device for hotswap (0/1) (DANGEROUS)\n
            -X      Set IDE xfer mode (DANGEROUS)\n
            -y      Put IDE drive in standby mode\n
            -Y      Put IDE drive to sleep\n
            -Z      Disable Seagate auto-powersaving mode\n
            -z      Re-read partition table</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_head"><strong>head      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    head       [OPTION]... [FILE]...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Print first 10 lines of each FILE to standard output.\n
    With more than one FILE, precede each with a header giving the\n
    file name. With no FILE, or when FILE is -, read standard input.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -n NUM  Print first NUM lines instead of first 10\n
            -c NUM  Output the first NUM bytes\n
            -q      Never output headers giving file names\n
            -v      Always output headers giving file names</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ head -n 2 /etc/passwd\n
            root:x:0:0:root:/root:/bin/bash\n
            daemon:x:1:1:daemon:/usr/sbin:/bin/sh</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_hexdump"><strong>hexdump   </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    hexdump    [-[bcCdefnosvx]] [OPTION] FILE\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Display <code>file(s)</code> or standard input in a user specified format</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -b              One-byte octal display\n
            -c              One-byte character display\n
            -C              Canonical hex+ASCII, 16 bytes per line\n
            -d              Two-byte decimal display\n
            -e FORMAT STRING\n
            -f FORMAT FILE\n
            -n LENGTH       Interpret only length bytes of input\n
            -o              Two-byte octal display\n
            -s OFFSET       Skip offset bytes\n
            -v              Display all input data\n
            -x              Two-byte hexadecimal display</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n

    </dd>\n

    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_init"><strong>init      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    init\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Init is the parent of all processes</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>This version of init is designed to be run only by the kernel.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>BusyBox init doesn't support multiple runlevels. The runlevels field of\n
    the /etc/inittab file is completely ignored by BusyBox init. If you want\n
    runlevels, use sysvinit.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>BusyBox init works just fine without an inittab. If no inittab is found,\n
    it has the following default behavior:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        ::sysinit:/etc/init.d/rcS\n
            ::askfirst:/bin/sh\n
            ::ctrlaltdel:/sbin/reboot\n
            ::shutdown:/sbin/swapoff -a\n
            ::shutdown:/bin/umount -a -r\n
            ::restart:/sbin/init</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>if it detects that /dev/console is _not_ a serial console, it will also run:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        tty2::askfirst:/bin/sh\n
            tty3::askfirst:/bin/sh\n
            tty4::askfirst:/bin/sh</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>If you choose to use an /etc/inittab file, the inittab entry format is as follows:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        &lt;id&gt;:&lt;runlevels&gt;:&lt;action&gt;:&lt;process&gt;</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        &lt;id&gt;:</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>                WARNING: This field has a non-traditional meaning for BusyBox init!\n
                    The id field is used by BusyBox init to specify the controlling tty for\n
                    the specified process to run on. The contents of this field are\n
                    appended to "/dev/" and used as-is. There is no need for this field to\n
                    be unique, although if it isn't you may have strange results. If this\n
                    field is left blank, the controlling tty is set to the console. Also\n
                    note that if BusyBox detects that a serial console is in use, then only\n
                    entries whose controlling tty is either the serial console or /dev/null\n
                    will be run. BusyBox init does nothing with utmp. We don't need no\n
                    stinkin' utmp.</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        &lt;runlevels&gt;:</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>                The runlevels field is completely ignored.</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        &lt;action&gt;:</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>                Valid actions include: sysinit, respawn, askfirst, wait,\n
                    once, restart, ctrlaltdel, and shutdown.</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>                The available actions can be classified into two groups: actions\n
                    that are run only once, and actions that are re-run when the specified\n
                    process exits.</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>                Run only-once actions:</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>                        'sysinit' is the first item run on boot. init waits until all\n
                            sysinit actions are completed before continuing. Following the\n
                            completion of all sysinit actions, all 'wait' actions are run.\n
                            'wait' actions, like 'sysinit' actions, cause init to wait until\n
                            the specified task completes. 'once' actions are asynchronous,\n
                            therefore, init does not wait for them to complete. 'restart' is\n
                            the action taken to restart the init process. By default this should\n
                            simply run /sbin/init, but can be a script which runs pivot_root or it\n
                            can do all sorts of other interesting things. The 'ctrlaltdel' init\n
                            actions are run when the system detects that someone on the system\n
                            console has pressed the CTRL-ALT-DEL key combination. Typically one\n
                            wants to run 'reboot' at this point to cause the system to reboot.\n
                            Finally the 'shutdown' action specifies the actions to taken when\n
                            init is told to reboot. Unmounting filesystems and disabling swap\n
                            is a very good here.</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>                Run repeatedly actions:</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>                        'respawn' actions are run after the 'once' actions. When a process\n
                            started with a 'respawn' action exits, init automatically restarts\n
                            it. Unlike sysvinit, BusyBox init does not stop processes from\n
                            respawning out of control. The 'askfirst' actions acts just like\n
                            respawn, except that before running the specified process it\n
                            displays the line "Please press Enter to activate this console."\n
                            and then waits for the user to press enter before starting the\n
                            specified process.</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>                Unrecognized actions (like initdefault) will cause init to emit an\n
                    error message, and then go along with its business. All actions are\n
                    run in the order they appear in /etc/inittab.</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        &lt;process&gt;:</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>                Specifies the process to be executed and its command line.</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example /etc/inittab file:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        # This is run first except when booting in single-user mode\n
            #\n
            ::sysinit:/etc/init.d/rcS\n
            \n
            # /bin/sh invocations on selected ttys\n
            #\n
            # Start an "askfirst" shell on the console (whatever that may be)\n
            ::askfirst:-/bin/sh\n
            # Start an "askfirst" shell on /dev/tty2-4\n
            tty2::askfirst:-/bin/sh\n
            tty3::askfirst:-/bin/sh\n
            tty4::askfirst:-/bin/sh\n
            \n
            # /sbin/getty invocations for selected ttys\n
            #\n
            tty4::respawn:/sbin/getty 38400 tty4\n
            tty5::respawn:/sbin/getty 38400 tty5\n
            \n
            \n
            # Example of how to put a getty on a serial line (for a terminal)\n
            #\n
            #::respawn:/sbin/getty -L ttyS0 9600 vt100\n
            #::respawn:/sbin/getty -L ttyS1 9600 vt100\n
            #\n
            # Example how to put a getty on a modem line\n
            #::respawn:/sbin/getty 57600 ttyS2\n
            \n
            # Stuff to do when restarting the init process\n
            ::restart:/sbin/init\n
            \n
            # Stuff to do before rebooting\n
            ::ctrlaltdel:/sbin/reboot\n
            ::shutdown:/bin/umount -a -r\n
            ::shutdown:/sbin/swapoff -a</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_insmod"><strong>insmod    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    insmod     [OPTION]... MODULE [symbol=value]...\n

    <dd>\n

    </dd>\n

            -k      Make module autoclean-able\n
            -v      Verbose\n
            -q      Quiet\n
            -L      Lock to prevent simultaneous loads of a module\n
            -m      Output load map to stdout\n
            -o NAME Set internal module name to NAME\n
            -x      Do not export externs</pre>\n
    </dd>\n

    </td></tr><tr><td></td><td>[dev STRING] [to PREFIX] }</td></tr></tbody></table>\n

    </dd>\n

    <p>The upper-case options MQS are used to remove a shared memory segment by a\n

            -[qQ]   Remove the message queue\n
            -[sS]   Remove the semaphore</pre>\n
    </dd>\n

    <dt><strong><a name="item_ipcs"><strong>ipcs      </strong></a></strong><br>\n

    Resource specification:</pre>\n

            -s      Semaphore arrays\n

    <dt><strong><a name="item_iproute"><strong>iproute   </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"><tbody><tr><td>iproute    { list | flush | { add | del | change | append |\n
    </td></tr><tr><td></td><td>replace | monitor } ROUTE }</td></tr></tbody></table>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>iproute { list | flush } SELECTOR\n
    iproute get ADDRESS [from ADDRESS iif STRING]</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>                        [oif STRING]  [tos TOS]\n
    iproute { add | del | change | append | replace | monitor } ROUTE</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>                        SELECTOR := [root PREFIX] [match PREFIX] [proto RTPROTO]\n
                            ROUTE := [TYPE] PREFIX [tos TOS] [proto RTPROTO]</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n

    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    iprule     {[list | add | del] RULE}\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n

    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        SELECTOR := [from PREFIX] [to PREFIX] [tos TOS] [fwmark FWMARK]\n
                            [dev STRING] [pref NUMBER]\n
            ACTION := [table TABLE_ID] [nat ADDRESS]\n
                            [prohibit | reject | unreachable]\n
                            [realms [SRCREALM/]DSTREALM]\n
            TABLE_ID := [local | main | default | NUMBER]</pre>\n
    </dd>\n

    </td></tr><tr><td></td><td>[remote ADDR] [local ADDR] [ttl TTL]</td></tr></tbody></table>\n

    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n

            252 root     root     S [apache]\n
            263 www-data www-data S [apache]\n
            264 www-data www-data S [apache]\n
            265 www-data www-data S [apache]\n
            266 www-data www-data S [apache]\n
            267 www-data www-data S [apache]\n
            $ kill 252</pre>\n

    redirects, job control, can be used as the shell for scripts, and has a\n

    Bourne Shell syntax. If you need things like ``if-then-else'', ``while'', and such\n

    </dd>\n

    </dt>\n

    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Create a link named LINK_NAME or DIRECTORY to the specified TARGET.\n
    You may use '--' to indicate that all following arguments are non-options.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -s      Make symlinks instead of hardlinks\n
            -f      Remove existing destination files\n
            -n      Don't dereference symlinks - treat like normal file\n
            -b      Make a backup of the target (if exists) before link operation\n
            -S suf  Use suffix instead of ~ when making backup files</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ ln -s BusyBox /tmp/ls\n
            $ ls -l /tmp/ls\n
            lrwxrwxrwx    1 root     root            7 Apr 12 18:39 ls -&gt; BusyBox*</pre>\n

    </td></tr><tr><td></td><td>losetup [<strong>-f</strong>] - show</td></tr></tbody></table>\n
    </dd>\n

    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>No arguments will display all current associations.\n
    One argument (losetup /dev/loop1) will display the current association\n
    (if any), or disassociate it (with -d). The display shows the offset\n
    and filename of the file the loop device is currently bound to.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Two arguments (losetup /dev/loop1 file.img) create a new association,\n
    with an optional offset (-o 12345). Encryption is not yet supported.\n
    losetup -f will show the first loop free loop device</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_ls"><strong>ls        </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    ls         [<strong>-1AacCdeFilnpLRrSsTtuvwxXhkK</strong>] [filenames...]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>List directory contents</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -1      List files in a single column\n
            -A      Do not list implied . and ..\n
            -a      Do not hide entries starting with .\n
            -C      List entries by columns\n
            -c      With -l: show ctime\n
            --color[={always,never,auto}]   Control coloring\n
            -d      List directory entries instead of contents\n
            -e      List both full date and full time\n
            -F      Append indicator (one of */=@|) to entries\n
            -i      List the i-node for each file\n
            -l      Use a long listing format\n
            -n      List numeric UIDs and GIDs instead of names\n
            -p      Append indicator (one of /=@|) to entries\n
            -L      List entries pointed to by symlinks\n
            -R      List subdirectories recursively\n
            -r      Sort the listing in reverse order\n
            -S      Sort the listing by file size\n
            -s      List the size of each file, in blocks\n
            -T NUM  Assume Tabstop every NUM columns\n
            -t      With -l: show modification time\n
            -u      With -l: show access time\n
            -v      Sort the listing by version\n
            -w NUM  Assume the terminal is NUM columns wide\n
            -x      List entries by lines instead of by columns\n
            -X      Sort the listing by extension\n
            -h      Print sizes in human readable format (e.g., 1K 243M 2G)\n
            -k      Print security context\n
            -K      Print security context in long format\n
            -Z      Print security context and permission</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
