    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_makedevs"><strong>makedevs  </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    makedevs   [<strong>-d</strong> device_table] rootdir\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Create a range of special files as specified in a device table.\n
    Device table entries take the form of:\n
    &lt;type&gt; &lt;mode&gt; &lt;uid&gt; &lt;gid&gt; &lt;major&gt; &lt;minor&gt; &lt;start&gt; &lt;inc&gt; &lt;count&gt;\n
    Where name is the file name, type can be one of:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        f       A regular file\n
            d       Directory\n
            c       Character special device file\n
            b       Block special device file\n
            p       Fifo (named pipe)\n
    uid is the user id for the target file, gid is the group id for the\n
    target file. The rest of the entries (major, minor, etc) apply to\n
    to device special files. A '-' may be used for blank entries.</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        For example:\n
            &lt;name&gt;    &lt;type&gt; &lt;mode&gt;&lt;uid&gt;&lt;gid&gt;&lt;major&gt;&lt;minor&gt;&lt;start&gt;&lt;inc&gt;&lt;count&gt;\n
            /dev         d   755    0    0    -      -      -      -    -\n
            /dev/console c   666    0    0    5      1      -      -    -\n
            /dev/null    c   666    0    0    1      3      0      0    -\n
            /dev/zero    c   666    0    0    1      5      0      0    -\n
            /dev/hda     b   640    0    0    3      0      0      0    -\n
            /dev/hda     b   640    0    0    3      1      1      1    15\n
            \n
            Will Produce:\n
            /dev\n
            /dev/console\n
            /dev/null\n
            /dev/zero\n
            /dev/hda\n
            /dev/hda[0-15]</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_matchpathcon"><strong>matchpathcon</strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    matchpathcon [<strong>-n</strong>] [<strong>-N</strong>] [<strong>-f</strong> file_contexts_file] [<strong>-p</strong> prefix] [<strong>-V</strong>]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -n      Do not display path\n
            -N      Do not use translations\n
            -f      Use alternate file_context file\n
            -p      Use prefix to speed translations\n
            -V      Verify file context on disk matches defaults</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_md5sum"><strong>md5sum    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    md5sum     [OPTION] [FILEs...]\n
       or: md5sum [OPTION] <strong>-c</strong> [FILE]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Print or check MD5 checksums</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:\n
    With no FILE, or when FILE is -, read standard input.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -c      Check MD5 sums against given list</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>The following two options are useful only when verifying checksums:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -s      Don't output anything, status code shows success\n
            -w      Warn about improperly formatted MD5 checksum lines</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ md5sum &lt; busybox\n
            6fd11e98b98a58f64ff3398d7b324003\n
            $ md5sum busybox\n
            6fd11e98b98a58f64ff3398d7b324003  busybox\n
            $ md5sum -c -\n
            6fd11e98b98a58f64ff3398d7b324003  busybox\n
            busybox: OK\n
            ^D</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_mdev"><strong>mdev      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    mdev       [<strong>-s</strong>]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -s      Scan /sys and populate /dev during system boot</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Called with no options (via hotplug) it uses environment variables\n
    to determine which device to add/remove.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>         The mdev config file contains lines that look like:\n
      hd[a-z][0-9]* 0:3 660</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>That's device name (with regex match), uid:gid, and permissions.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Optionally, that can be followed (on the same line) by a special character\n
    and a command line to run after creating/before deleting the corresponding\n
    device(s). The environment variable $MDEV indicates the active device node\n
    (which is useful if it's a regex match). For example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>  hdc root:cdrom 660  *ln -s $MDEV cdrom</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>The special characters are @ (run after creating), $ (run before deleting),\n
    and * (run both after creating and before deleting). The commands run in\n
    the /dev directory, and use <code>system()</code> which calls /bin/sh.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Config file parsing stops on the first matching line. If no config\n
    entry is matched, devices are created with default 0:0 660. (Make\n
    the last line match .* to override this.)</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_mesg"><strong>mesg      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    mesg       [y|n]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Control write access to your terminal</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        y       Allow write access to your terminal\n
            n       Disallow write access to your terminal</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_microcom"><strong>microcom  </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    microcom   [<strong>-s</strong> speed] tty-name\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_mkdir"><strong>mkdir     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    mkdir      [OPTION] DIRECTORY...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Create the <code>DIRECTORY(ies)</code> if they do not already exist</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -m      Set permission mode (as in chmod), not rwxrwxrwx - umask\n
            -p      No error if existing, make parent directories as needed\n
            -Z      Set security context</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ mkdir /tmp/foo\n
            $ mkdir /tmp/foo\n
            /tmp/foo: File exists\n
            $ mkdir /tmp/foo/bar/baz\n
            /tmp/foo/bar/baz: No such file or directory\n
            $ mkdir -p /tmp/foo/bar/baz</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_mke2fs"><strong>mke2fs    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    mke2fs     [<strong>-c</strong>|<strong>-l</strong> filename] [<strong>-b</strong> block-size] [<strong>-f</strong> fragment-size] [<strong>-g</strong> blocks-per-group] [<strong>-i</strong> bytes-per-inode] [<strong>-j</strong>] [<strong>
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -b size         Block size in bytes\n
            -c              Check for bad blocks before creating\n
            -E opts         Set extended options\n
            -f size         Fragment size in bytes\n
            -F              Force (ignore sanity checks)\n
            -g num          Number of blocks in a block group\n
            -i ratio        The bytes/inode ratio\n
            -j              Create a journal (ext3)\n
            -J opts         Set journal options (size/device)\n
            -l file         Read bad blocks list from file\n
            -L lbl          Set the volume label\n
            -m percent      Percent of fs blocks to reserve for admin\n
            -M dir          Set last mounted directory\n
            -n              Do not actually create anything\n
            -N num          Number of inodes to create\n
            -o os           Set the 'creator os' field\n
            -O features     Dir_index/filetype/has_journal/journal_dev/sparse_super\n
            -q              Quiet\n
            -r rev          Set filesystem revision\n
            -S              Write superblock and group descriptors only\n
            -T fs-type      Set usage type (news/largefile/largefile4)\n
            -v              Verbose</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_mkfifo"><strong>mkfifo    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    mkfifo     [OPTIONS] name\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Create a named pipe (identical to 'mknod name p')</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -m      Create the pipe using the specified mode (default a=rw)\n
            -Z      Set security context</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_mkfs_2eminix"><strong>mkfs.minix</strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    mkfs.minix [<strong>-c</strong> | <strong>-l</strong> filename] [<strong>-nXX</strong>] [<strong>-iXX</strong>] /dev/name [blocks]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Make a MINIX filesystem</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -c              Check device for bad blocks\n
            -n [14|30]      Maximum length of filenames\n
            -i INODES       Number of inodes for the filesystem\n
            -l FILENAME     Read bad blocks list from FILENAME\n
            -v              Make a Minix version 2 filesystem</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_mknod"><strong>mknod     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    mknod      [OPTIONS] NAME TYPE MAJOR MINOR\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Create a special file (block, character, or pipe)</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -m      Create the special file using the specified mode (default a=rw)</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>TYPEs include:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        b:      Make a block (buffered) device\n
            c or u: Make a character (un-buffered) device\n
            p:      Make a named pipe. MAJOR and MINOR are ignored for named pipes\n
            -Z      Set security context</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ mknod /dev/fd0 b 2 0\n
            $ mknod -m 644 /tmp/pipe p</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_mkswap"><strong>mkswap    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    mkswap     [<strong>-c</strong>] [<strong>-v0</strong>|<strong>-v1</strong>] device [block-count]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Prepare a disk partition to be used as swap partition</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -c              Check for read-ability\n
            -v0             Make version 0 swap [max 128 Megs]\n
            -v1             Make version 1 swap [big!] (default for kernels &gt; 2.1.117)\n
            block-count     Number of block to use (default is entire partition)</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_mktemp"><strong>mktemp    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    mktemp     [<strong>-dq</strong>] TEMPLATE\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Create a temporary file with its name based on TEMPLATE.\n
    TEMPLATE is any name with six 'Xs' (i.e., /tmp/temp.XXXXXX).</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -d      Make a directory instead of a file\n
            -q      Fail silently if an error occurs</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ mktemp /tmp/temp.XXXXXX\n
            /tmp/temp.mWiLjM\n
            $ ls -la /tmp/temp.mWiLjM\n
            -rw-------    1 andersen andersen        0 Apr 25 17:10 /tmp/temp.mWiLjM</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_modprobe"><strong>modprobe  </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    modprobe   [<strong>-knqrsv</strong>] MODULE [symbol=value ...]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -k      Make module autoclean-able\n
            -n      Just show what would be done\n
            -q      Quiet\n
            -r      Remove module (stacks) or do autoclean\n
            -s      Report via syslog instead of stderr\n
            -v      Verbose</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>modprobe can (un)load a stack of modules, passing each module options (when\n
    loading). modprobe uses a configuration file to determine what <code>option(s)</code> to\n
    pass each module it loads.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>The configuration file is searched (in order) amongst:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>    /etc/modprobe.conf (2.6 only)\n
        /etc/modules.conf\n
        /etc/conf.modules (deprecated)</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>They all have the same syntax (see below). If none is present, it is\n
    _not_ an error; each loaded module is then expected to load without\n
    options. Once a file is found, the others are tested for.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>/etc/modules.conf entry format:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>  alias &lt;alias_name&gt; &lt;mod_name&gt;\n
        Makes it possible to modprobe alias_name, when there is no such module.\n
        It makes sense if your mod_name is long, or you want a more representative\n
        name for that module (eg. 'scsi' in place of 'aha7xxx').\n
        This makes it also possible to use a different set of options (below) for\n
        the module and the alias.\n
        A module can be aliased more than once.</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>  options &lt;mod_name|alias_name&gt; &lt;symbol=value ...&gt;\n
        When loading module mod_name (or the module aliased by alias_name), pass\n
        the "symbol=value" pairs as option to that module.</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Sample /etc/modules.conf file:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>  options tulip irq=3\n
      alias tulip tulip2\n
      options tulip2 irq=4 io=0x308</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Other functionality offered by 'classic' modprobe is not available in\n
    this implementation.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>If module options are present both in the config file, and on the command line,\n
    then the options from the command line will be passed to the module _after_\n
    the options from the config file. That way, you can have defaults in the config\n
    file, and override them for a specific usage from the command line.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        (with the above /etc/modules.conf):\n
            \n
            $ modprobe tulip\n
               will load the module 'tulip' with default option 'irq=3'\n
            \n
            $ modprobe tulip irq=5\n
               will load the module 'tulip' with option 'irq=5', thus overriding the default\n
            \n
            $ modprobe tulip2\n
               will load the module 'tulip' with default options 'irq=4 io=0x308',\n
               which are the default for alias 'tulip2'\n
            \n
            $ modprobe tulip2 irq=8\n
               will load the module 'tulip' with default options 'irq=4 io=0x308 irq=8',\n
               which are the default for alias 'tulip2' overridden by the option 'irq=8'\n
            \n
               from the command line\n
            \n
            $ modprobe tulip2 irq=2 io=0x210\n
               will load the module 'tulip' with default options 'irq=4 io=0x308 irq=4 io=0x210',\n
               which are the default for alias 'tulip2' overridden by the options 'irq=2 io=0x210'\n
            \n
               from the command line</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_more"><strong>more      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    more       [FILE ...]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>View FILE or standard input one screenful at a time</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ dmesg | more</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_mount"><strong>mount     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    mount      [flags] DEVICE NODE [<strong>-o</strong> options,more-options]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Mount a filesystem. Filesystem autodetection requires /proc be mounted.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -a              Mount all filesystems in fstab\n
            -f              "Fake" Add entry to mount table but don't mount it\n
            -n              Don't write a mount table entry\n
            -o option       One of many filesystem options, listed below\n
            -r              Mount the filesystem read-only\n
            -t fs-type      Filesystem type\n
            -w              Mount for reading and writing (default)</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options for use with the ``<strong>-o</strong>'' flag:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        loop            Ignored (loop devices are autodetected)\n
            [a]sync         Writes are asynchronous / synchronous\n
            [no]atime       Disable / enable updates to inode access times\n
            [no]diratime    Disable / enable atime updates to directories\n
            [no]dev         Allow use of special device files / disallow them\n
            [no]exec        Allow use of executable files / disallow them\n
            [no]suid        Allow set-user-id-root programs / disallow them\n
            [r]shared       Convert [recursively] to a shared subtree\n
            [r]slave        Convert [recursively] to a slave subtree\n
            [r]private      Convert [recursively] to a private subtree\n
            [un]bindable    Make mount point [un]able to be bind mounted\n
            bind            Bind a directory to an additional location\n
            move            Relocate an existing mount point\n
            remount         Remount a mounted filesystem, changing its flags\n
            ro/rw           Mount for read-only / read-write</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>There are EVEN MORE flags that are specific to each filesystem\n
    You'll have to see the written documentation for those filesystems</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Returns 0 for success, number of failed mounts for -a, or errno for one mount.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ mount\n
            /dev/hda3 on / type minix (rw)\n
            proc on /proc type proc (rw)\n
            devpts on /dev/pts type devpts (rw)\n
            $ mount /dev/fd0 /mnt -t msdos -o ro\n
            $ mount /tmp/diskimage /opt -t ext2 -o loop\n
            $ mount cd_image.iso mydir</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_mountpoint"><strong>mountpoint</strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    mountpoint [<strong>-q</strong>] &lt;[<strong>-d</strong>] DIR | <strong>-x</strong> DEVICE&gt;\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>mountpoint checks if the directory is a mountpoint</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -q      Quiet\n
            -d      Print major/minor device number of the filesystem\n
            -x      Print major/minor device number of the blockdevice</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ mountpoint /proc\n
            /proc is not a mountpoint\n
            $ mountpoint /sys\n
            /sys is a mountpoint</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_mt"><strong>mt        </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    mt         [<strong>-f</strong> device] opcode value\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Control magnetic tape drive operation</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Available Opcodes:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>bsf bsfm bsr bss datacompression drvbuffer eof eom erase\n
    fsf fsfm fsr fss load lock mkpart nop offline ras1 ras2\n
    ras3 reset retension rewind rewoffline seek setblk setdensity\n
    setpart tell unload unlock weof wset</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_mv"><strong>mv        </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    mv         [OPTION]... SOURCE DEST\n
    or: mv [OPTION]... SOURCE... DIRECTORY\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Rename SOURCE to DEST, or move <code>SOURCE(s)</code> to DIRECTORY</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -f      Don't prompt before overwriting\n
            -i      Interactive, prompt before overwrite</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ mv /tmp/foo /bin/bar</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_nameif"><strong>nameif    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    nameif     [<strong>-s</strong>] [<strong>-c</strong> FILE] [{IFNAME MACADDR}]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Rename network interface while it in the down state</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -c FILE         Use configuration file (default is /etc/mactab)\n
            -s              Use syslog (LOCAL0 facility)\n
            IFNAME MACADDR  new_interface_name interface_mac_address</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ nameif -s dmz0 00:A0:C9:8C:F6:3F\n
             or\n
            $ nameif -c /etc/my_mactab_file</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_nc"><strong>nc        </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    nc         [<strong>-options</strong>] hostname port  - connect\n
    nc [<strong>-options</strong>] <strong>-l</strong> <strong>-p</strong> port [hostname] [port]  - listen\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>         -l             Listen mode, for inbound connects\n
    B&lt;-n&gt;           Do not do DNS resolution\n
    B&lt;-s&gt; addr              Local address\n
    B&lt;-p&gt; port              Local port\n
    B&lt;-u&gt;           UDP mode\n
    B&lt;-v&gt;           Verbose (cumulative: B&lt;-vv&gt;)\n
    B&lt;-w&gt; secs              Timeout for connects and final net reads\n
    B&lt;-i&gt; sec               Delay interval for lines sent" /* ", ports scanned" */ \n
    B&lt;-o&gt; file              Hex dump of traffic\n
    B&lt;-z&gt;           Zero-I/O mode (scanning)\n
    B&lt;-e&gt; prog [args]       Program to exec after connect (must be last)/*   "\n
    B&lt;-r&gt;           Randomize local and remote ports" */</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>         To use netcat as a terminal emulator on a serial port:</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>$ stty 115200 -F /dev/ttyS0\n
    $ stty raw -echo -ctlecho &amp;&amp; nc -f /dev/ttyS0</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ nc foobar.somedomain.com 25\n
            220 foobar ESMTP Exim 3.12 #1 Sat, 15 Apr 2000 00:03:02 -0600\n
            help\n
            214-Commands supported:\n
            214-    HELO EHLO MAIL RCPT DATA AUTH\n
            214     NOOP QUIT RSET HELP\n
            quit\n
            221 foobar closing connection</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_netstat"><strong>netstat   </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    netstat    [<strong>-laentuwxrW</strong>]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Display networking information</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -l      Display listening server sockets\n
            -a      Display all sockets (default: connected)\n
            -e      Display other/more information\n
            -n      Don't resolve names\n
            -t      Tcp sockets\n
            -u      Udp sockets\n
            -w      Raw sockets\n
            -x      Unix sockets\n
            -r      Display routing table\n
            -W      Display with no column truncation</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_nice"><strong>nice      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    nice       [<strong>-n</strong> ADJUST] [COMMAND [ARG] ...]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Run a program with modified scheduling priority</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -n ADJUST       Adjust the scheduling priority by ADJUST</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_nmeter"><strong>nmeter    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    nmeter     format_string\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Monitor system in real time</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p></p><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"><tbody><tr><td>Format specifiers:\n
    </td></tr><tr><td>%Nc or %[cN]</td><td>Monitor CPU. N - bar size, default 10</td></tr></tbody></table>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>                (displays: S:system U:user N:niced D:iowait I:irq i:softirq)\n
    %[niface]       Monitor network interface 'iface'\n
    %m              Monitor allocated memory\n
    %[mf]           Monitor free memory\n
    %[mt]           Monitor total memory\n
    %s              Monitor allocated swap\n
    %f              Monitor number of used file descriptors\n
    %Ni             Monitor total/specific IRQ rate\n
    %x              Monitor context switch rate\n
    %p              Monitor forks\n
    %[pn]           Monitor # of processes\n
    %b              Monitor block io\n
    %Nt             Show time (with N decimal points)\n
    %Nd             Milliseconds between updates (default=1000)\n
    %r              Print &lt;cr&gt; instead of &lt;lf&gt; at EOL</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        nmeter '%250d%t %20c int %i bio %b mem %m forks%p'</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_nohup"><strong>nohup     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    nohup      COMMAND [ARGS]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Run a command immune to hangups, with output to a non-tty</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ nohup make &amp;</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_nslookup"><strong>nslookup  </strong></a></strong><br>\n

    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_passwd"><strong>passwd    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    passwd     [OPTION] [name]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Change a user password. If no name is specified,\n
    changes the password for the current user.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -a      Define which algorithm shall be used for the password\n
                    (choices: des, md5)\n
    " /* ", sha1)" */       B&lt;-d&gt;   Delete the password for the specified user account</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -l      Locks (disables) the specified user account\n
            -u      Unlocks (re-enables) the specified user account</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_patch"><strong>patch     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    patch      [<strong>-p</strong> num] [<strong>-i</strong> diff]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -p NUM  Strip NUM leading components from file names\n
            -i DIFF Read DIFF instead of stdin</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ patch -p1 &lt; example.diff\n
            $ patch -p0 -i example.diff</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_pgrep"><strong>pgrep     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    pgrep      [<strong>-flnovx</strong>] pattern\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Display <code>process(es)</code> selected by regex pattern</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -l      Show command name too\n
            -f      Match against entire command line\n
            -n      Signal the newest process only\n
            -o      Signal the oldest process only\n
            -v      Negate the matching\n
            -x      Match whole name (not substring)</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_pidof"><strong>pidof     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    pidof      process-name [OPTION] [process-name ...]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>List the PIDs of all processes with names that match the\n
    names on the command line</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        USAGE_PIDOF      \n
            -s      Display only a single PID\n
            -o PID  Omit given pid\n
                    Use %PPID to omit the parent pid of pidof itself</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ pidof init\n
            1\n
            $ pidof /bin/sh\n
            20351 5973 5950\n
            $ pidof /bin/sh -o %PPID\n
            20351 5950</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_ping"><strong>ping      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    ping       [OPTION]... host\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Send ICMP ECHO_REQUEST packets to network hosts</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -4, -6          Force IPv4 or IPv6 hostname resolution\n
            -c CNT          Send only CNT pings\n
            -s SIZE         Send SIZE data bytes in packets (default=56)\n
            -I iface/IP     Use interface or IP address as source\n
            -q              Quiet, only displays output at start\n
                            and when finished</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ ping localhost\n
            PING slag (127.0.0.1): 56 data bytes\n
            64 bytes from 127.0.0.1: icmp_seq=0 ttl=255 time=20.1 ms\n
            \n
            --- debian ping statistics ---\n
            1 packets transmitted, 1 packets received, 0% packet loss\n
            round-trip min/avg/max = 20.1/20.1/20.1 ms</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_ping6"><strong>ping6     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    ping6      [OPTION]... host\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Send ICMP ECHO_REQUEST packets to network hosts</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -c CNT          Send only CNT pings\n
            -s SIZE         Send SIZE data bytes in packets (default=56)\n
            -I iface/IP     Use interface or IP address as source\n
            -q              Quiet, only displays output at start\n
                            and when finished</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ ping6 ip6-localhost\n
            PING ip6-localhost (::1): 56 data bytes\n
            64 bytes from ::1: icmp6_seq=0 ttl=64 time=20.1 ms\n
            \n
            --- ip6-localhost ping statistics ---\n
            1 packets transmitted, 1 packets received, 0% packet loss\n
            round-trip min/avg/max = 20.1/20.1/20.1 ms</pre>\n
    </dd>\n

    <dt><strong><a name="item_run_2dparts"><strong>run-parts </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    run-parts  [<strong>-t</strong>] [<strong>-l</strong>] [<strong>-a</strong> ARG] [<strong>-u</strong> MASK] DIRECTORY\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Run a bunch of scripts in a directory</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -t      Prints what would be run, but does not actually run anything\n
            -a ARG  Pass ARG as an argument for every program invoked\n
            -u MASK Set the umask to MASK before executing every program\n
            -l      Prints names of all matching files even when they are not executable</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ run-parts -a start /etc/init.d\n
            $ run-parts -a stop=now /etc/init.d\n
            \n
            Let's assume you have a script foo/dosomething:\n
            #!/bin/sh\n
            for i in $*; do eval $i; done; unset i\n
            case "$1" in\n
            start*) echo starting something;;\n
            stop*) set -x; shutdown -h $stop;;\n
            esac\n
            \n
            Running this yields:\n
            $run-parts -a stop=+4m foo/\n
            + shutdown -h +4m</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_runcon"><strong>runcon    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"><tbody><tr><td>runcon     [<strong>-c</strong>] [<strong>-u</strong> USER] [<strong>-r</strong> ROLE] [<strong>-t</strong> TYPE] [<strong>-l</strong> RANGE] COMMAND [args]\n
    </td></tr><tr><td></td><td>runcon CONTEXT COMMAND [args]</td></tr></tbody></table>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>runcon [<strong>-c</strong>] [<strong>-u</strong> USER] [<strong>-r</strong> ROLE] [<strong>-t</strong> TYPE] [<strong>-l</strong> RANGE] COMMAND [args]\n
    runcon CONTEXT COMMAND [args]\n
    Run a program in a different security context</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        CONTEXT         Complete security context\n
            -c, --compute   Compute process transition context before modifying\n
            -t, --type=TYPE Type (for same role as parent)\n
            -u, --user=USER User identity\n
            -r, --role=ROLE Role\n
            -l, --range=RNG Levelrange</pre>\n
    </dd>\n

    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_sed"><strong>sed       </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    sed        [<strong>-efinr</strong>] pattern [files...]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -e script       Add the script to the commands to be executed\n
            -f scriptfile   Add script-file contents to the\n
                            commands to be executed\n
            -i              Edit files in-place\n
            -n              Suppress automatic printing of pattern space\n
            -r              Use extended regular expression syntax</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>If no <strong>-e</strong> or <strong>-f</strong> is given, the first non-option argument is taken as the sed\n
    script to interpret. All remaining arguments are names of input files; if no\n
    input files are specified, then the standard input is read. Source files\n
    will not be modified unless <strong>-i</strong> option is given.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ echo "foo" | sed -e 's/f[a-zA-Z]o/bar/g'\n
            bar</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_selinuxenabled"><strong>selinuxenabled</strong></a></strong><br>\n

    </dd>\n

    <dd>\n
    setfiles   [<strong>-dnpqsvW</strong>] [<strong>-e</strong> dir]... [<strong>-o</strong> filename] [<strong>-r</strong> alt_root_path] [<strong>-c</strong> policyfile] spec_file pathname\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Reset file contexts under pathname according to spec_file</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -c file Check the validity of the contexts against the specified binary policy\n
            -d      Show which specification matched each file\n
            -l      Log changes in file labels to syslog\n
            -n      Don't change any file labels\n
            -q      Suppress warnings\n
            -r dir  Use an altenate root path\n
            -e dir  Exclude directory\n
            -F      Force reset of context to match file_context for customizable files\n
            -o file Save list of files with incorrect context\n
            -s      Take a list of files from standard input (instead of command line)\n
            -v      Show changes in file labels, if type or role are changing\n
            -vv     Show changes in file labels, if type, role, or user are changing\n
            -W      Display warnings about entries that had no matching files</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_setkeycodes"><strong>setkeycodes</strong></a></strong><br>\n

    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Set entries into the kernel's scancode-to-keycode map,\n
    allowing unusual keyboards to generate usable keycodes.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n

    </dd>\n

    </dd>\n

    <dt><strong><a name="item_slattach"><strong>slattach  </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    slattach   [<strong>-cehmLF</strong>] [<strong>-s</strong> speed] [<strong>-p</strong> protocol] DEVICEs\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Attach network <code>interface(s)</code> to serial <code>line(s)</code></p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -p      Set protocol (slip, cslip, slip6, clisp6 or adaptive)\n
            -s      Set line speed\n
            -e      Exit after initializing device\n
            -h      Exit when the carrier is lost\n
            -c      Execute a command when the line is hung up\n
            -m      Do NOT initialize the line in raw 8 bits mode\n
            -L      Enable 3-wire operation\n
            -F      Disable RTS/CTS flow control</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_sleep"><strong>sleep     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    sleep      [N]...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>                 Pause for a time equal to the total of the args given, where each arg can\n
    have an optional suffix of (s)econds, (m)inutes, (h)ours, or (d)ays</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ sleep 2\n
            [2 second delay results]\n
            $ sleep 1d 3h 22m 8s\n
            [98528 second delay results]</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_softlimit"><strong>softlimit </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    softlimit  [<strong>-a</strong> allbytes] [<strong>-c</strong> corebytes] [<strong>-d</strong> databytes] [<strong>-f</strong> filebytes] [<strong>-l</strong> lockbytes] [<strong>-m</strong> membytes] [<strong>-o</strong> openfiles] [<stro
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Set soft resource limits, then run prog</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -m n    Same as -d n -s n -l n -a n\n
            -d n    Limit the data segment per process to n bytes\n
            -s n    Limit the stack segment per process to n bytes\n
            -l n    Limit the locked physical pages per process to n bytes\n
            -a n    Limit the total of all segments per process to n bytes\n
            -o n    Limit the number of open file descriptors per process to n\n
            -p n    Limit the number of processes per uid to n\n
    Options controlling file sizes:</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -f n    Limit output file sizes to n bytes\n
            -c n    Limit core file sizes to n bytes\n
    Efficiency opts:</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -r n    Limit the resident set size to n bytes. This limit is not\n
                    enforced unless physical memory is full\n
            -t n    Limit the CPU time to n seconds. This limit is not enforced\n
                    except that the process receives a SIGXCPU signal after n seconds</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Some options may have no effect on some operating systems\n
    n may be =, indicating that soft limit should be set equal to hard limit</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_sort"><strong>sort      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    sort       [<strong>-nrugMcszbdfimSTokt</strong>] [<strong>-o</strong> outfile] [<strong>-k</strong> start[.offset][opts][,end[.offset][opts]] [<strong>-t</strong> char] [FILE]...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Sort lines of text in the specified files</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -b      Ignore leading blanks\n
            -c      Check whether input is sorted\n
            -d      Dictionary order (blank or alphanumeric only)\n
            -f      Ignore case\n
            -g      General numerical sort\n
            -i      Ignore unprintable characters\n
            -k      Sort key\n
            -M      Sort month\n
            -n      Sort numbers\n
            -o      Output to file\n
            -k      Sort by key\n
            -t      Use key separator other than whitespace\n
            -r      Reverse sort order\n
            -s      Stable (don't sort ties alphabetically)\n
            -u      Suppress duplicate lines\n
            -z      Input terminated by nulls, not newlines\n
            -mST    Ignored for GNU compatibility</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ echo -e "e\nf\nb\nd\nc\na" | sort\n
            a\n
            b\n
            c\n
            d\n
            e\n
            f\n
            $ echo -e "c 3\nb 2\nd 2" | $SORT -k 2,2n -k 1,1r\n
            d 2\n
            b 2\n
            c 3</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_split"><strong>split     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    split      [OPTION] [INPUT [PREFIX]]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -b n[k|m]       Split by bytes\n
            -l n            Split by lines\n
            -a n            Use n letters as suffix</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ split TODO foo\n
            $ cat TODO | split -a 2 -l 2 TODO_</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_start_2dstop_2ddaemon"><strong>start-stop-daemon</strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    start-stop-daemon [OPTIONS] [-<strong>-start</strong>|-<strong>-stop</strong>] ... [-- arguments...]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Start and stop services</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -S|--start                      Start\n
            -K|--stop                       Stop\n
            -a|--startas pathname           Starts process specified by pathname\n
            -b|--background                 Put process into background\n
            -u|--user username|uid          Stop this user's processes\n
            -x|--exec executable            Program to either start or check\n
            -m|--make-pidfile               Create the -p file and enter pid in it\n
            -n|--name process-name          Stop processes with this name\n
            -p|--pidfile pid-file           Save or load pid using a pid-file\n
            -q|--quiet                      Quiet\n
            -o|--oknodo                     Exit status 0 if nothing done\n
            -v|--verbose                    Verbose\n
            -N|--nicelevel N                Add N to process's nice level\n
            -s|--signal signal              Signal to send (default TERM)\n
            -c|--chuid user[:[group]]       Change to specified user/group</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_stat"><strong>stat      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    stat       [OPTION] FILE...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Display file (default) or filesystem status</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -c fmt  Use the specified format\n
            -f      Display filesystem status\n
            -L,-l   Dereference links\n
            -t      Display info in terse form\n
            -Z      Print security context</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Valid format sequences for files:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre> %a     Access rights in octal\n
     %A     Access rights in human readable form\n
     %b     Number of blocks allocated (see %B)\n
     %B     The size in bytes of each block reported by %b\n
     %d     Device number in decimal\n
     %D     Device number in hex\n
     %f     Raw mode in hex\n
     %F     File type\n
     %g     Group ID of owner\n
     %G     Group name of owner\n
     %h     Number of hard links\n
     %i     Inode number\n
     %n     File name\n
     %N     Quoted file name with dereference if symlink\n
     %o     I/O block size\n
     %s     Total size, in bytes\n
     %t     Major device type in hex\n
     %T     Minor device type in hex\n
     %u     User ID of owner\n
     %U     User name of owner\n
     %x     Time of last access\n
     %X     Time of last access as seconds since Epoch\n
     %y     Time of last modification\n
     %Y     Time of last modification as seconds since Epoch\n
     %z     Time of last change\n
     %Z     Time of last change as seconds since Epoch</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Valid format sequences for file systems:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre> %a     Free blocks available to non-superuser\n
     %b     Total data blocks in file system\n
     %c     Total file nodes in file system\n
     %d     Free file nodes in file system\n
     %f     Free blocks in file system\n
     %C     Security context in SELinux\n
     %i     File System ID in hex\n
     %l     Maximum length of filenames\n
     %n     File name\n
     %s     Block size (for faster transfer)\n
     %S     Fundamental block size (for block counts)\n
     %t     Type in hex\n
     %T     Type in human readable form</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_strings"><strong>strings   </strong></a></strong><br>\n

    strings    [<strong>-afo</strong>] [<strong>-n</strong> length] [file ...]\n
    </dd>\n

            -o      Each string is preceded by its decimal offset in the file</pre>\n

    <dt><strong><a name="item_sv"><strong>sv        </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    sv         [<strong>-v</strong>] [<strong>-w</strong> sec] command service...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Control services monitored by runsv supervisor.\n
    Commands (only first character is enough):</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>status: query service status\n
    up: if service isn't running, start it. If service stops, restart it\n
    once: like 'up', but if service stops, don't restart it\n
    down: send TERM and CONT signals. If ./run exits, start ./finish</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>    if it exists. After it stops, do not restart service\n
    exit: send TERM and CONT signals to service and log service. If they exit,</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>    runsv exits too\n
    pause, cont, hup, alarm, interrupt, quit, 1, 2, term, kill: send\n
    STOP, CONT, HUP, ALRM, INT, QUIT, USR1, USR2, TERM, KILL signal to service</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_svlogd"><strong>svlogd    </strong></a></strong><br>\n

    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_sysctl"><strong>sysctl    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    sysctl     [OPTIONS]... [VALUE]...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Configure kernel parameters at runtime</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -n      Use this option to disable printing of the key name when printing values\n
            -w      Use this option when you want to change a sysctl setting\n
            -p      Load in sysctl settings from the file specified or /etc/sysctl.conf if none given\n
            -a      Display all values currently available\n
            -A      Display all values currently available in table form</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        sysctl [-n] variable ...\n
            sysctl [-n] -w variable=value ...\n
            sysctl [-n] -a\n
            sysctl [-n] -p file     (default /etc/sysctl.conf)\n
            sysctl [-n] -A</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_syslogd"><strong>syslogd   </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    syslogd    [OPTION]...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>System logging utility.\n
    Note that this version of syslogd ignores /etc/syslog.conf.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -n              Run in foreground\n
            -O FILE         Log to given file (default=/var/log/messages)\n
            -l n            Set local log level\n
            -S              Smaller logging output\n
            -s SIZE         Max size (KB) before rotate (default=200KB, 0=off)\n
            -b NUM          Number of rotated logs to keep (default=1, max=99, 0=purge)\n
            -R HOST[:PORT]  Log to IP or hostname on PORT (default PORT=514/UDP)\n
            -L              Log locally and via network (default is network only if -R)\n
            -C[size(KiB)]   Log to shared mem buffer (read it using logread)</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ syslogd -R masterlog:514\n
            $ syslogd -R 192.168.1.1:601</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_tail"><strong>tail      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    tail       [OPTION]... [FILE]...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Print last 10 lines of each FILE to standard output.\n
    With more than one FILE, precede each with a header giving the\n
    file name. With no FILE, or when FILE is -, read standard input.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -c N[kbm]       Output the last N bytes\n
            -n N[kbm]       Print last N lines instead of last 10\n
            -f              Output data as the file grows\n
            -q              Never output headers giving file names\n
            -s SEC          Wait SEC seconds between reads with -f\n
            -v              Always output headers giving file names</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>If the first character of N (bytes or lines) is a '+', output begins with\n
    the Nth item from the start of each file, otherwise, print the last N items\n
    in the file. N bytes may be suffixed by k (x1024), b (x512), or m (1024^2).</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ tail -n 1 /etc/resolv.conf\n
            nameserver 10.0.0.1</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_tar"><strong>tar       </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    tar        -[czjaZxtvO] [<strong>-X</strong> FILE] [<strong>-f</strong> TARFILE] [<strong>-C</strong> DIR] [FILE(s)] ...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Create, extract, or list files from a tar file</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        c       Create\n
            x       Extract\n
            t       List</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Archive format selection:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        z       Filter the archive through gzip\n
            j       Filter the archive through bzip2\n
            a       Filter the archive through lzma\n
            Z       Filter the archive through compress</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>File selection:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        f       Name of TARFILE or "-" for stdin\n
            O       Extract to stdout\n
            exclude File to exclude\n
            X       File with names to exclude\n
            C       Change to directory DIR before operation\n
            v       Verbose</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ zcat /tmp/tarball.tar.gz | tar -xf -\n
            $ tar -cf /tmp/tarball.tar /usr/local</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_taskset"><strong>taskset   </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    taskset    [OPTIONS] [mask] [pid | command [arg]...]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Set or get CPU affinity</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -p      Operate on an existing PID</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ taskset 0x7 ./dgemm_test&amp;\n
            $ taskset -p 0x1 $!\n
            pid 4790's current affinity mask: 7\n
            pid 4790's new affinity mask: 1\n
            $ taskset 0x7 /bin/sh -c './taskset -p 0x1 $$'\n
            pid 6671's current affinity mask: 1\n
            pid 6671's new affinity mask: 1\n
            $ taskset -p 1\n
            pid 1's current affinity mask: 3</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_tcpsvd"><strong>tcpsvd    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    tcpsvd     [<strong>-hEv</strong>] [<strong>-c</strong> n] [<strong>-C</strong> n:msg] [<strong>-b</strong> n] [<strong>-u</strong> user] [<strong>-l</strong> name] ip port prog...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Creates TCP socket, binds it to ip:port and listens on it\n
    for incoming connections. For each connection it runs prog.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p></p><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"><tbody><tr><td>ip</td><td>IP to listen on. '0' = all\n
    </td></tr><tr><td>port</td><td>Port to listen on\n
    </td></tr><tr><td>prog [arg]</td><td>Program to run\n
    </td></tr><tr><td><strong>-l</strong> name</td><td>Local hostname (else looks up local hostname in DNS)\n
    </td></tr><tr><td><strong>-u</strong> user[:group]</td><td>Change to user/group after bind\n
    </td></tr><tr><td><strong>-c</strong> n</td><td>Handle up to n connections simultaneously\n
    </td></tr><tr><td><strong>-b</strong> n</td><td>Allow a backlog of approximately n TCP SYNs\n
    </td></tr><tr><td><strong>-C</strong> n[:msg]</td><td>Allow only up to n connections from the same IP</td></tr></tbody></table>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>                New connections from this IP address are closed\n
                    immediately. 'msg' is written to the peer before close\n
    B&lt;-h&gt;           Look up peer's hostname\n
    B&lt;-E&gt;           Do not set up environment variables\n
    B&lt;-v&gt;           Verbose</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_tee"><strong>tee       </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    tee        [OPTION]... [FILE]...\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Copy standard input to each FILE, and also to standard output</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -a      Append to the given FILEs, do not overwrite\n
            -i      Ignore interrupt signals (SIGINT)</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ echo "Hello" | tee /tmp/foo\n
            $ cat /tmp/foo\n
            Hello</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_telnet"><strong>telnet    </strong></a></strong><br>\n

    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Connect to remote telnet server</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n

    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Handle incoming telnet connections</p>\n
    </dd>\n

    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_test"><strong>test      </strong></a></strong><br>\n

      or   [ EXPRESSION ]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n

    determined by the value of EXPRESSION</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n

    <pre>        $ test 1 -eq 2\n
            $ echo $?\n
            1\n
            $ test 1 -eq 1\n
            $ echo $?\n
            0\n
            $ [ -d /etc ]\n
            $ echo $?\n
            0\n
            $ [ -d /junk ]\n
            $ echo $?\n
            1</pre>\n
    </dd>\n

    <dt><strong><a name="item_touch"><strong>touch     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    touch      [<strong>-c</strong>] FILE [FILE ...]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Update the last-modified date on the given FILE[s]</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n

    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ ls -l /tmp/foo\n
            /bin/ls: /tmp/foo: No such file or directory\n
            $ touch /tmp/foo\n
            $ ls -l /tmp/foo\n
            -rw-rw-r--    1 andersen andersen        0 Apr 15 01:11 /tmp/foo</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_tr"><strong>tr        </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    tr         [<strong>-cds</strong>] STRING1 [STRING2]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Translate, squeeze, and/or delete characters from\n
    standard input, writing to standard output</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -c      Take complement of STRING1\n
            -d      Delete input characters coded STRING1\n
            -s      Squeeze multiple output characters of STRING2 into one character</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ echo "gdkkn vnqkc" | tr [a-y] [b-z]\n
            hello world</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_traceroute"><strong>traceroute</strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"><tbody><tr><td>traceroute [<strong>-FIldnrv</strong>] [<strong>-f</strong> 1st_ttl] [<strong>-m</strong> max_ttl] [<strong>-p</strong> port#] [<strong>-q</strong> nqueries]\n
    </td></tr><tr><td></td><td>[<strong>-s</strong> src_addr] [<strong>-t</strong> tos] [<strong>-w</strong> wait] [<strong>-g</strong> gateway] [<strong>-i</strong> iface]\n
    </td></tr><tr><td></td><td>[<strong>-z</strong> pausemsecs] host [data size]</td></tr></tbody></table>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Trace the route to ``host</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -F      Set the don't fragment bit\n
            -I      Use ICMP ECHO instead of UDP datagrams\n
            -l      Display the ttl value of the returned packet\n
            -d      Set SO_DEBUG options to socket\n
            -n      Print hop addresses numerically rather than symbolically\n
            -r      Bypass the normal routing tables and send directly to a host\n
            -v      Verbose\n
            -m max_ttl      Max time-to-live (max number of hops)\n
            -p port#        Base UDP port number used in probes\n
                            (default is 33434)\n
            -q nqueries     Number of probes per 'ttl' (default 3)\n
            -s src_addr     IP address to use as the source address\n
            -t tos          Type-of-service in probe packets (default 0)\n
            -w wait         Time in seconds to wait for a response\n
                            (default 3 sec)\n
            -g              Loose source route gateway (8 max)</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n

    </dd>\n

    <dt><strong><a name="item_udhcpc"><strong>udhcpc    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"><tbody><tr><td>udhcpc     [<strong>-Cfbnqtv</strong>] [<strong>-c</strong> CID] [<strong>-V</strong> VCLS] [<strong>-H</strong> HOSTNAME] [<strong>-i</strong> INTERFACE]\n
    </td></tr><tr><td></td><td>[<strong>-p</strong> pidfile] [<strong>-r</strong> IP] [<strong>-s</strong> script]</td></tr></tbody></table>\n

            -s,--script=file        Run file at dhcp events (default: /usr/share/udhcpc/default.script)\n
            -t,--retries=N          Send up to N request packets\n
            -f,--foreground Run in foreground\n
            -b,--background Background if lease cannot be immediately negotiated\n
            -S,--syslog     Log to syslog too\n

    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Creates UDP socket, binds it to ip:port and listens on it\n
    for incoming packets. For each packet it runs prog\n
    (redirecting all further packets with same peer ip:port to it).</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p></p><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"><tbody><tr><td>ip</td><td>IP to listen on. '0' = all\n
    </td></tr><tr><td>port</td><td>Port to listen on\n
    </td></tr><tr><td>prog [arg]</td><td>Program to run\n
    </td></tr><tr><td><strong>-l</strong> name</td><td>Local hostname (else looks up local hostname in DNS)\n
    </td></tr><tr><td><strong>-u</strong> user[:group]</td><td>Change to user/group after bind\n
    </td></tr><tr><td><strong>-c</strong> n</td><td>Handle up to n connections simultaneously\n
    </td></tr><tr><td><strong>-h</strong></td><td>Look up peer's hostname\n
    </td></tr><tr><td><strong>-E</strong></td><td>Do not set up environment variables\n
    </td></tr><tr><td><strong>-v</strong></td><td>Verbose</td></tr></tbody></table>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_umount"><strong>umount    </strong></a></strong><br>\n

    </dd>\n

    </dd>\n

    <p>Options:</p>\n

            -n      Don't erase /etc/mtab entries\n
            -r      Try to remount devices as read-only if mount is busy\n
            -l      Lazy umount (detach filesystem)\n
            -f      Force umount (i.e., unreachable NFS server)\n
            -D      Do not free loop device (if a loop device has been used)</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n

    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    unexpand   [<strong>-f</strong>][<strong>-a</strong>][<strong>-t</strong> NUM] [FILE|-]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n

    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n

    </dd>\n

    <pre>        -a,--all        Convert all blanks\n
            -f,--first-only Convert only leading sequences of blanks\n
            -t,--tabs=N     Tabstops every N chars</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_uniq"><strong>uniq      </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    uniq       [<strong>-fscdu</strong>]... [INPUT [OUTPUT]]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Discard all but one of successive identical lines from INPUT\n
    (or standard input), writing to OUTPUT (or standard output)</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -c      Prefix lines by the number of occurrences\n
            -d      Only print duplicate lines\n
            -u      Only print unique lines\n
            -f N    Skip the first N fields\n
            -s N    Skip the first N chars (after any skipped fields)</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ echo -e "a\na\nb\nc\nc\na" | sort | uniq\n
            a\n
            b\n
            c</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_unix2dos"><strong>unix2dos  </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    unix2dos   [option] [FILE]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Convert FILE from unix format to dos format. When no option\n
    is given, the input is converted to the opposite output format.\n
    When no file is given, use stdin/stdout.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -u      Output will be in UNIX format\n
            -d      Output will be in DOS format</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_unlzma"><strong>unlzma    </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    unlzma     [OPTION]... [FILE]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Uncompress FILE (or standard input if FILE is '-' or omitted)</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -c      Write output to standard output\n
            -f      Force</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_unzip"><strong>unzip     </strong></a></strong><br>\n
    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    unzip      [<strong>-opts</strong>[modifiers]] file[.zip] [list] [<strong>-x</strong> xlist] [<strong>-d</strong> exdir]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Extract files from ZIP archives</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -l      List archive contents (with -q for short form)\n
            -n      Never overwrite existing files (default)\n
            -o      Overwrite files without prompting\n
            -p      Send output to stdout\n
            -q      Quiet\n
            -x      Exclude these files\n
            -d      Extract files into this directory</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n
    <dt><strong><a name="item_uptime"><strong>uptime    </strong></a></strong><br>\n

              1:55pm  up  2:30, load average: 0.09, 0.04, 0.00</pre>\n

    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n

    NB: finds outfile name in uuencoded source unless <strong>-o</strong> is given</p>\n
    </dd>\n

    </dd>\n

    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n

            begin 755 busybox\n

    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n

    more than one FILE is specified. With no FILE, read standard input.</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -c      Print the byte counts\n
            -l      Print the newline counts\n
            -L      Print the length of the longest line\n
            -w      Print the word counts</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n

                 31      46    1365 /etc/passwd</pre>\n
    </dd>\n

    <dd>\n
    <table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"><tbody><tr><td>wget       [<strong>-c</strong>|-<strong>-continue</strong>] [<strong>-s</strong>|-<strong>-spider</strong>] [<strong>-q</strong>|-<strong>-quiet</strong>] [<strong>-O</strong>|-<strong
    </td></tr><tr><td></td><td>[-<strong>-header</strong> 'header: value'] [<strong>-Y</strong>|-<strong>-proxy</strong> on/off] [<strong>-P</strong> DIR]\n

    </dd>\n

            -q      Quiet\n
            -P      Set directory prefix to DIR\n

            -Y      Use proxy ('on' or 'off')</pre>\n

    </dt>\n
    <dd>\n
    xargs      [OPTIONS] [COMMAND] [ARGS...]\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Execute COMMAND on every item given by standard input</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Options:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        -p      Prompt the user about whether to run each command\n
            -r      Do not run command for empty read lines\n
            -x      Exit if the size is exceeded\n
            -0      Input filenames are terminated by a null character\n
            -t      Print the command line on stderr before executing it</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <p>Example:</p>\n
    </dd>\n
    <dd>\n
    <pre>        $ ls | xargs gzip\n
            $ find . -name '*.c' -print | xargs rm</pre>\n
    </dd>\n
    <p></p>\n

    </dd>\n

    <hr>\n
    <h1><a name="libc_nss">LIBC NSS</a></h1>\n
    <p>GNU Libc (glibc) uses the Name Service Switch (NSS) to configure the behavior\n
    of the C library for the local environment, and to configure how it reads\n
    system data, such as passwords and group information.  This is implemented\n
    using an /etc/nsswitch.conf configuration file, and using one or more of the\n
    /lib/libnss_* libraries.  BusyBox tries to avoid using any libc calls that make\n
    use of NSS.  Some applets however, such as login and su, will use libc functions\n
    that require NSS.</p>\n
    <p>If you enable CONFIG_USE_BB_PWD_GRP, BusyBox will use internal functions to\n
    directly access the /etc/passwd, /etc/group, and /etc/shadow files without\n
    using NSS.  This may allow you to run your system without the need for\n
    installing any of the NSS configuration files and libraries.</p>\n
    <p>When used with glibc, the BusyBox 'networking' applets will similarly require\n
    that you install at least some of the glibc NSS stuff (in particular,\n
    /etc/nsswitch.conf, /lib/libnss_dns*, /lib/libnss_files*, and /lib/libresolv*).</p>\n
    <p>Shameless Plug: As an alternative, one could use a C library such as uClibc.  In\n
    addition to making your system significantly smaller, uClibc does not require the\n
    use of any NSS support files or libraries.</p>\n
    <p>\n
    </p>\n
